      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Gabon" title="Languages of Gabon">
        Languages of Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       It is
       <a href="/wiki/African_French#note-2007_report" title="African French">
        estimated that 80%
       </a>
       of Gabon's population can speak French, and that 30% of Libreville residents are native speakers of the language. Nationally, 32% of the Gabonese people speak the
       <a href="/wiki/Fang_language" title="Fang language">
        Fang language
       </a>
       as a mother tongue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 2012, just before the 14th summit of the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
       </a>
       , the country declared an intention to add English as a second official language, reportedly in response to an investigation by France into corruption in the African country,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-independent-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       though a government spokesman insisted it was for practical reasons only.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was later clarified that the country intended to introduce English as a first foreign language in schools, while keeping French as the general medium of instruction and the sole official language.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Gabon" title="Religion in Gabon">
        Religion in Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Major religions practiced in Gabon include
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestantism
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Bwiti" title="Bwiti">
        Bwiti
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       , and indigenous
       <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">
        animistic
       </a>
       religion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-report_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-report-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many persons practice elements of both Christianity and traditional indigenous religious beliefs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-report_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-report-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Approximately 73 percent of the population, including noncitizens, practice at least some elements of Christianity, including the syncretistic Bwiti; 12 percent practice Islam (of whom 80 to 90 percent are foreigners); 10 percent practice traditional indigenous religious beliefs exclusively; and 5 percent practice no religion or are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheists" title="Atheists">
        atheists
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-report_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-report-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A vivid description of taboos and magic is provided by Schweitzer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Health">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Gabon" title="Health in Gabon">
        Health in Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most of the health services of Gabon are public, but there are some private institutions, of which the best known is the hospital established in 1913 in
       <a href="/wiki/Lambar%C3%A9n%C3%A9" title="Lambaréné">
        Lambaréné
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Schweitzer" title="Albert Schweitzer">
        Albert Schweitzer
       </a>
       . Gabon's medical infrastructure is considered one of the best in
       <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
        West Africa
       </a>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2016)">
           by whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . By 1985 there were 28 hospitals, 87 medical centers, and 312 infirmaries and dispensaries. As of 2004
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , there were an estimated 29 physicians per 100,000 people. Approximately 90% of the population had access to health care services.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2000, 70% of the population had access to safe drinking water and 21% had adequate sanitation. A comprehensive government health program treats such diseases as
       <a href="/wiki/Leprosy" title="Leprosy">
        leprosy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">
        sleeping sickness
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">
        malaria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Filariasis" title="Filariasis">
        filariasis
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intestinal_worms" title="Intestinal worms">
        intestinal worms
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">
        tuberculosis
       </a>
       . Rates for immunization of children under the age of one were 97% for tuberculosis and 65% for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">
        polio
       </a>
       . Immunization rates for
       <a href="/wiki/DPT_vaccine" title="DPT vaccine">
        DPT
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">
        measles
       </a>
       were 37% and 56% respectively. Gabon has a domestic supply of pharmaceuticals from a factory in Libreville.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">
        total fertility rate
       </a>
       has decreased from 5.8 in 1960 to 4.2 children per mother during childbearing years in 2000. Ten percent of all births were low birth weight. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality_rate" title="Maternal mortality rate">
        maternal mortality rate
       </a>
       was 520 per 100,000 live births as of 1998. In 2005, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate">
        infant mortality rate
       </a>
       was 55.35 per 1,000 live births and life expectancy was 55.02 years. As of 2002, the overall mortality rate was estimated at 17.6 per 1,000 inhabitants.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">
        HIV/AIDS
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">
        prevalence
       </a>
       is estimated to be 5.2% of the adult population (ages 15–49).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2009
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , approximately 46,000 people were living with HIV/AIDS.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There were an estimated 2,400 deaths from AIDS in 2009 – down from 3,000 deaths in 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Gabon" title="Education in Gabon">
        Education in Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Gabon's education system is regulated by two ministries: the Ministry of Education, in charge of pre-kindergarten through the last high school grade, and the Ministry of Higher Education and Innovative Technologies, in charge of universities, higher education, and professional schools.
      </p>
      <p>
       Education is compulsory for children ages 6 to 16 under the Education Act. Most children in Gabon start their school lives by attending nurseries or "Crèche", then kindergarten known as "Jardins d'Enfants". At age 6, they are enrolled in primary school, "École Primaire" which is made up of six grades. The next level is "École Secondaire", which is made up of seven grades. The planned graduation age is 19 years old. Those who graduate can apply for admission at institutions of higher learning, including engineering schools or business schools. Gabon's literacy rate is 83.2%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cinnwk_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cinnwk-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The government has used oil revenue for school construction, paying teachers' salaries, and promoting education, including in rural areas. However, maintenance of school structures, as well as teachers' salaries, has been declining. In 2002 the gross primary enrollment rate was 132 percent, and in 2000 the net primary enrollment rate was 78 percent. Gross and net enrollment ratios are based on the number of students formally registered in primary school and therefore do not necessarily reflect actual school attendance. As of 2001, 69 percent of children who started primary school were likely to reach grade 5. Problems in the education system include poor management and planning, lack of oversight, poorly qualified teachers, and overcrowded classrooms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ilab-20">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TsogoMask.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="853" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TsogoMask.jpg/220px-TsogoMask.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TsogoMask.jpg/330px-TsogoMask.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/TsogoMask.jpg/440px-TsogoMask.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TsogoMask.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Gabonese mask
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Gabon" title="Culture of Gabon">
        Culture of Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       A country with a primarily
       <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">
        oral tradition
       </a>
       up until the spread of literacy in the 21st century, Gabon is rich in
       <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">
        folklore
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mythology" title="Mythology">
        mythology
       </a>
       . "Raconteurs" are currently working to keep traditions alive such as the mvett among the Fangs and the ingwala among the Nzebis.
      </p>
      <p>
       Gabon also features internationally celebrated masks, such as the n'goltang (Fang) and the relicary figures of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kota_people_(Gabon)" title="Kota people (Gabon)">
        Kota
       </a>
       . Each group has its own set of masks used for various reasons. They are mostly used in traditional ceremonies such as marriage, birth and funerals. Traditionalists mainly work with rare local woods and other precious materials.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Gabon" title="Music of Gabon">
        Music of Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Gabonese music is lesser-known in comparison with regional giants like the
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
        Democratic Republic of the Congo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">
        Cameroon
       </a>
       . The country boasts an array of folk styles, as well as pop stars like
       <a href="/wiki/Patience_Dabany" title="Patience Dabany">
        Patience Dabany
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Annie-Flore_Batchiellilys" title="Annie-Flore Batchiellilys">
        Annie-Flore Batchiellilys
       </a>
       , a Gabonese singer and renowned live performer. Also known are guitarists like Georges Oyendze, La Rose Mbadou and Sylvain Avara, and the singer
       <a href="/wiki/Oliver_N%27Goma" title="Oliver N'Goma">
        Oliver N'Goma
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Imported rock and hip hop from the US and UK are popular in Gabon, as are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_Rumba" title="Cuban Rumba">
        rumba
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">
        makossa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">
        soukous
       </a>
       . Gabonese folk instruments include the obala, the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ngombi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ngombi (page does not exist)">
        ngombi
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/ngombi" title="fr:ngombi">
         fr
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Balafon" title="Balafon">
        balafon
       </a>
       and traditional drums.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Gabon" title="Media of Gabon">
        Media of Gabon
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Radio-Diffusion Télévision Gabonaise (RTG), which is owned and operated by the government, broadcasts in
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       and indigenous languages. Color television broadcasts have been introduced in major cities. In 1981, a commercial radio station, Africa No. 1, began operations. The most powerful radio station on the continent, it has participation from the French and Gabonese governments and private European media.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2004, the government operated two radio stations and another seven were privately owned. There were also two government television stations and four privately owned. In 2003, there were an estimated 488 radios and 308 television sets for every 1,000 people. About 11.5 of every 1,000 people were cable subscribers. Also in 2003, there were 22.4 personal computers for every 1,000 people and 26 of every 1,000 people had access to the
       <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">
        Internet
       </a>
       . The national press service is the Gabonese Press Agency, which publishes a daily paper,
       <i>
        Gabon-Matin
       </i>
       (circulation 18,000 as of 2002).
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/L%27Union" title="L'Union">
         L'Union
        </a>
       </i>
       in Libreville, the government-controlled daily newspaper, had an average daily circulation of 40,000 in 2002. The weekly
       <i>
        Gabon d'Aujourdhui
       </i>
       is published by the Ministry of Communications. There are about nine privately owned periodicals which are either independent or affiliated with political parties. These publish in small numbers and are often delayed by financial constraints. The constitution of Gabon provides for free speech and a free press, and the government supports these rights. Several periodicals actively criticize the government and foreign publications are widely available.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gabon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon_national_football_team" title="Gabon national football team">
        Gabon national football team
       </a>
       has represented the nation since 1962.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon_national_under-23_football_team" title="Gabon national under-23 football team">
        Under-23 football team
       </a>
       won the
       <a href="/wiki/2011_CAF_U-23_Championship" title="2011 CAF U-23 Championship">
        2011 CAF U-23 Championship
       </a>
       and qualified for the
       <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament">
        2012 London Olympics
       </a>
       . Gabon were joint hosts, along with
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">
        Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
       , of the
       <a href="/wiki/2012_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 Africa Cup of Nations">
        2012 Africa Cup of Nations
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the sole hosts of the competition's
       <a href="/wiki/2017_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2017 Africa Cup of Nations">
        2017 tournament
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon_national_basketball_team" title="Gabon national basketball team">
        Gabon national basketball team
       </a>
       , nicknamed
       <i>
        Les Panthères
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       finished 8th at the
       <a href="/wiki/AfroBasket_2015" title="AfroBasket 2015">
        AfroBasket 2015
       </a>
       , its best performance ever.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon_at_the_Olympics" title="Gabon at the Olympics">
        Gabon
       </a>
       has competed at most Summer Olympics since 1972. The country's sole Olympic medalist is
       <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Obame" title="Anthony Obame">
        Anthony Obame
       </a>
       , won a silver in
       <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">
        taekwondo
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">
        2012 Olympics
       </a>
       , held in London.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
